for each cluster, including both RELICS observations and archival data from other proposals.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs3-2\" name=\"apjaabe7bs3-2\">3.2.\u00a0Imaging Data Reduction</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>All subexposures in each filter were combined to form a deep image using the AstroDrizzle package (Gonzaga et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib15\">2012</a>) using <tt>PIXFRAC</tt>\u00a0=\u00a00.8. The data in different filters were aligned to the same pixel frame, and the astrometry was corrected to match the Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer (WISE) point-source catalog (Wright et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib50\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib50\">2010</a>). Final drizzled images were generated in two pixel scales: 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />03 and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />06, for best sampling of the ACS and WFC3/IR point-spread functions, respectively. The ACS data were corrected for charge transfer inefficiency losses prior to drizzling. The final reduced data are <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"dataset\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://doi.org/10.17909/T9SP45\" data-art-data-content-type=\"External repository\" data-toolbar-link=\"https://doi.org/10.17909/T9SP45\" data-toolbar-title=\"MAST dataset\" data-art-data-type=\"ext-rep-mast\" id=\"https://doi.org/10.17909/T9SP45\">made available</a> to the public as high level science products through the Mikulski Archive for Space Telescopes (MAST).<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bfn2\">17</a></sup>\n\n</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs3-3\" name=\"apjaabe7bs3-3\">3.3.\u00a0Photometry Catalog</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The RELICS team has produced catalogs of photometry and photometric redshifts for each field, based on the final 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />06 data set. These catalogs are made available through MAST. A full description of the photometry data products will appear in a separate publication (D. Coe et al. 2018, in preparation). Sources are extracted from a weighted stack of all the data (ACS and WFC3/IR), and from a weighted stack of the WFC3/IR data alone using SExtractor (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib4\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib4\">1996</a>) version 2.8.6 in dual-image mode. The weighted stack image is used as the reference image in SExtractor for all seven filters. The fluxes and colors of sources are measured within isophotal apertures, and are corrected for Galactic extinction (Schlafly &amp; Finkbeiner <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib39\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib39\">2011</a>).</p><p>The photometric redshift (photo-<em>z</em>) of each galaxy is estimated using the BPZ algorithm (Bayesian Photometric Redshifts; Ben\u00edtez <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib2\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib2\">2000</a>; Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib10\">2006</a>; Benitez et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib3\">2014</a>). We run BPZ with 11 spectral energy distribution (SED) model templates (five ellipticals, two late types, and four starbursts) as described in Benitez et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib3\">2014</a>) and Rafelski et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib36\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib36\">2015</a>). The models are based on PEGASE, including emission lines (Fioc &amp; Rocca-Volmerange <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib13\">1997</a>). They are then recalibrated to match the observed photometry of galaxies with spectroscopic redshifts from FIREWORKS (Wuyts et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib51\">2008</a>). The BPZ algorithm redshifts these SEDs by fitting them to the observed photometry of each galaxy, using a Bayesian prior on redshift given the <em>i</em>-band magnitude and spectral type. The elliptical templates for galaxies at high redshifts are downweighted by the prior, and lower redshift solutions are generally preferred over those at higher redshifts. Possible lensing magnification is not considered in the prior.</p><p>Strongly lensed galaxies, particularly those used as constraints in this paper, were given further manual inspection. Several of these sources yielded less reliable photometric redshifts because they were fainter and/or contaminated by brighter nearby galaxies (usually cluster members). As a result, the photometric redshifts of multiple lensed images match one another often, but not always.</p><p>The system photo-<em>z</em> was manually determined by examining the redshift solution of all the images of the same system, where higher weight was given to images that are brighter and better isolated. We excluded any redshift solutions lower than the cluster redshift for systems that were identified as lensed sources to ensure that the model placed the source behind the cluster.</p></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs3-4\" name=\"apjaabe7bs3-4\">3.4.\u00a0Ground-based Spectroscopy</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Ground-based spectroscopic observations of RELICS clusters were conducted using the upgraded Low Dispersion Survey Spectrograph (LDSS3-C<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bfn3\">18</a></sup>\n) on the <em>Magellan</em> Clay telescope using time from the University of Michigan allocation (PI: Sharon) and the University of Arizona allocation (PI: Stark). The observations used multi-object slit masks, which had slits placed on candidate lensed galaxies at highest priority. The remaining slits were placed on cluster-member galaxies (selected by color) or other interesting objects in the cluster field, such as candidate ram-pressure stripping galaxies (e.g., Ebeling et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib12\">2014</a>) or candidate supernova hosts. We used the VPH-ALL grism, which has high sensitivity over the widest range of wavelengths: 4250 \u00c5 &lt; <em>\u03bb</em>\u00a0&lt; 10,000 \u00c5. This range is useful for the identification of emission lines at unknown redshifts. A 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />0 slit was used for all objects, which yielded a spectral resolution of R\u00a0450-1100 across that wavelength range.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bfn4\">19</a></sup>\n The detector covers a spatial extent of 6.4 arcmin.</p><p>Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt3\">3</a> provides the date of the observation and the exposure time for each field considered in this work. The spectroscopic data were reduced using the standard procedures using the COSMOS data reduction package.<sup xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"fnref\"><a class=\"fnref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bfn5\">20</a></sup>\n We report here on spectroscopic redshifts that were secured for candidate lensed galaxies and used as constraints in this paper. A full description of the results from these follow-up programs will be given in a future publication (R. Mainali et al. 2018, in preparation).</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt3\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 3.</b>\u00a0\nCluster Spectroscopy Observations\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bt3\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt3_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 3\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Cluster</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">Date</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Exposure Time, Notes</th>\n</tr>\n</thead><tbody>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Abell\u00a02163</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2016 Jun 07\u201308</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">1 hr</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Abell\u00a02537</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2016 Aug 02\u201303</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">2 masks, 1.5 hr each</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">RXC\u00a0J2211.7-0349</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2016 Aug 02\u201303</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">2 hr</td>\n</tr>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">ACT-CLJ0102-49151</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">2016 Aug 02\u201303</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">2 hr</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> Dates and exposure times for spectroscopic observations carried out with <em>Magellan</em>/LDSS3 on the clusters presented in this paper to date. The average seeing during integration for each cluster was 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />7, with the exception of ACT-CLJ0102, where the average seeing was 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />8.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt3_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaabe7bs4\" name=\"apjaabe7bs4\">4.\u00a0Strong Lensing Analysis</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We present the lens models for five galaxy clusters in the RELICS survey. The properties of these clusters are given in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt1\">1</a>.</p><p>Strong lens models were computed using <tt>Lenstool</tt> (Jullo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib21\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib21\">2007</a>), which models the cluster projected mass density as a combination of parametric halos. Each halo is modeled as a pseudo-isothermal ellipsoidal mass distribution (PIEMD; Limousin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib22\">2005</a>) and the best-fit set of parameters is found using Markov Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) sampling. The parameters that are allowed to vary in the modeling process are, for each halo, the <em>x</em> and <em>y</em> positions of the center of the halo; the ellipticity of the halo, <em>e</em>; its position angle, <em>\u03b8</em>; the core radius, <em>r</em><sub>core</sub>; the truncation radius of the cluster halo, <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub>; and the effective velocity dispersion, <em>\u03c3</em>. Optimization of the models presented in this paper was performed in the image plane.</p><p>Cluster-member galaxies were selected using the cluster red sequence method (Gladders &amp; Yee <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib14\">2000</a>) to have colors consistent with the red sequence at this redshift. Two bands that straddle the 4000 \u00c5 break were used for each cluster depending on redshift (F606W-F814W for Abell 2163 and RXC J2211.7-0349; F814W-F105W for Abell 2537; F435W-F814W for RXC J0142.9+4438; F105W-F140W for ACT-CLJ0102-49151). The brightest 100 galaxies were used for Abell\u00a02163, Abell\u00a02537, and ACT-CLJ0102-49151, while the brightest 166 galaxies were used for RXC\u00a0J2211.7-0349 and the brightest 200 galaxies were used for RXC\u00a0J0142.9+4438.</p><p>The selected cluster galaxies were modeled as PIEMD halos. Following Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib22\">2005</a>), the core radius of the cluster-member galaxies was fixed at 0.15 kpc, and <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub> and <em>\u03c3</em> were scaled with the F814W luminosity, except for ACT-CLJ0102-49151, for which the F105W band was used. The positional parameters (<em>x</em>, <em>y</em>, <em>e</em>, <em>\u03b8</em>) were fixed to the properties of their light distribution as measured with SExtractor (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib4\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib4\">1996</a>).</p><p>The strong lens models were constrained by identifying the positions of multiply imaged systems (\"arcs\"). Arcs are identified by eye as multiple images of the same background galaxy, based on their morphology, structure, and color. When we identify a system of arcs, we verify that the orientation and parity of each arc is consistent with the expectation from lensing. We assume an uncertainty of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />3 in the positions of each arc.</p><p>Several authors (e.g., Smith et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib42\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib42\">2009</a>; Johnson &amp; Sharon <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib19\">2016</a>) have shown that even with excellent positional constraints, such as the ones provided by <em>HST</em> imaging, the accuracy of strong lens models relies on the availability of redshift information of the lensed galaxies. In particular, models that lack redshift constraints are limited in their ability to correctly measure the slope of the mass distribution, and the lensing magnification derived from such models may be biased (Johnson &amp; Sharon <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib19\">2016</a>).</p><p>The RELICS program aims to provide the community with the best available lens models of all observed clusters in time to prepare for <em>JWST</em> observations. However, as of the release of this paper some clusters in the survey have no redshift constraints, some clusters have a spectroscopic redshift of only one lensed galaxy, and some have two or more spectroscopic redshifts. When spectroscopic information is unavailable, photometric redshifts can be used as constraints by setting limits on the redshift parameter. These limits are based on the probability distribution function of the photometric redshift analysis. However, catastrophic outliers might bias the result and force the model into a wrong solution, as shown in Johnson &amp; Sharon (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib19\">2016</a>). Thus it is advised that lens models that are not based on spectroscopic redshifts should be treated with caution.</p><p>To facilitate the release of lens models for all targeted clusters, including those with limited redshift constraints, we follow the procedure below when computing the lens models. The procedure aims to reduce the systematic error due to redshift uncertainty; to reduce the probability of a catastrophic photo-<em>z</em> outlier affecting the result; and to estimate the effect of the redshift uncertainty on deliverables, such as lensing magnification and mass.</p><p>Case\u00a01\u2014clusters with at least one spectroscopic redshift of multiply imaged lensed background sources (Abell 2537, RXC 2211): in this case, we use the spectroscopic redshift(s) as fixed constraint(s). The redshifts of arcs without spectroscopic redshifts are treated as free parameters. We use the photometric redshifts of these arcs as a guide to set the redshift prior on the lens model. However, following the recommendations of Johnson &amp; Sharon (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib19\">2016</a>), we allow broader limits than the photometric redshift probability distribution function so as not to be biased by catastrophic outliers.</p><p>Case\u00a02\u2014clusters with no spectroscopic redshifts of background sources (RXC 0142, ACT 0102, Abell 2163): in this case, we attempt to leave all the redshifts as free parameters. If this approach fails (e.g., results in unrealistic model-predicted redshifts or lensing mass), we fix the redshift of one of the lensed systems to its best-fit photo-<em>z</em>. We test the choice of which source to fix to ensure that it has a minor effect on other model choices. The redshifts of the remaining sources are left as free parameters, as in Case\u00a01.</p><p>In both cases, we test the agreement between the model-predicted redshifts (model-<em>z</em>) and the photo-<em>z</em> posterior. For a viable lens model, we require that there must not be a significant systematic bias between the model-<em>z</em> and the photo-<em>z</em>, i.e., that the agreement between model-<em>z</em> and photo-<em>z</em> is within the 1<em>\u03c3</em> uncertainties for most sources. Our procedure avoids introducing biases into the lens model due to photo-<em>z</em> modeling uncertainties or catastrophic outliers. In Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bs5\">5</a>, we quantify the effect of the redshift parameter on the uncertainties.</p><p>In the following sections, we describe each model in more detail. The results of the lens models, which include the mass and the effective Einstein radius, are given in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt4\">4</a>. In all the models, our numbering scheme of multiply imaged lensed sources lists the source number first, to the left of the decimal point, and the image number to the right of the decimal point. For example, three images of source galaxy #1 would be labeled 1.1, 1.2, and 1.3. Tables <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt5\">5</a>\u2013<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt14\">14</a> give the details of the lensed galaxies that were used as constraints and the parameters for each lens model, as well as the ID, coordinates, and photo-<em>z</em> of each image. Spectroscopic redshifts are given for sources for which those were measured. When one source is composed of multiple visually distinct clumps, or emission knots, photometric redshifts are listed separately for each individual knot.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt4\" Abell\u00a02537. The model-<em>z</em> and rms are given for the best-fit model, and the rms is measured in the image plane for each family of multiple images.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt5_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt5_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs4-1\" name=\"apjaabe7bs4-1\">4.1.\u00a0Abell\u00a02537</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We detect four lensed systems in the field of Abell\u00a02537, as described below (see also Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt5\">5</a>).</p><p>System #1 is lensed into four images. We identify three separate emission knots in this galaxy, designated as 1.1\u20131.4, 11.1\u201311.4, and 12.1\u201312.4 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf1\">1</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaabe7bf1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bf1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Left: image of Abell\u00a02537 created using a combination of WFC3IR imaging in the red (F160W) and ACS imaging in the green (F814W) and blue (F435W). Multiply imaged galaxies are labeled. The red curve marks the location of the critical curve for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0. A second critical curve is plotted in yellow at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0. The image is oriented northeast. Right: the magnification for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0 from the best-fit lens model is shown as contours; contour values are given in the legend. The background colormap indicates the uncertainty level in each location, given as \u0394<em>\u03bc</em>/<em>\u03bc</em>. The uncertainty estimate takes into account the source redshift uncertainty, but does not account for other systematics (see the text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaabe7bf1\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaabe7bf1\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>System #2 is lensed into four multiple images, each one containing two emission knots. The images are labeled 2.1\u20132.4 and 20.1\u201320.4 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf1\">1</a>. We measure a spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>\u00a0=\u00a03.611 for image 2.4, based on Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission in our LDSS3 spectroscopy (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bs3-4\">3.4</a>). This falls within the 95% CL range of the photometric redshifts of the image and is slightly lower than its highest probability peak (Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt5\">5</a>). We used the spectroscopic redshift as a fixed constraint in our lensing analysis.</p><p>System #3 has three multiple images. We identify three distinct emission knots in each image, labeled 3.1\u20133.3, 30.1\u201330.3, and 31.1\u201331.3 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf1\">1</a>. We find that not fixing a second redshift parameter in this cluster (in addition to the one spectroscopic redshift) causes the model to default to a nonphysical result, e.g., the model predicts redshifts higher than <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a013. We therefore fix the redshift of images 3.1\u20133.3 to the photometric redshift for this source, <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.2, in order to better constrain the lensing potential in the regions further away from the center of the cluster.</p><p>System #4 is a faint galaxy, labeled 4.1\u20134.2 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf1\">1</a>. The lensing analysis predicts additional images at two other locations within the field, but their predicted magnitudes are too faint to be detected, which explains their absence from the data.</p><p>The lens model for this cluster favors a combination of two cluster-scale halos, both located close to the center of the cluster within the strong lensing regime. As described above, we include perturbation from galaxy-scale halos. We allow the parameters of the cluster-scale halos to be solved for by the lens model. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt5\">5</a> lists the locations of the lensed galaxies and their redshifts. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt6\">6</a> lists the best-fit parameters of the resulting model.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt6\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 6.</b>\u00a0\nAbell\u00a02537 Model Parameters\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bt6\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt6_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 6\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">ID</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u0394R.A. The model-<em>z</em> and rms are given for the best-fit model, and the rms is measured in the image plane for each family of multiple images.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt7_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt7_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>System #1 is labeled 1.1\u20131.4 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf2\">2</a>. The photometric redshift for this system varies significantly between the four images, due to contamination from objects near images 1.3 and 1.4. The photometry of images 1.1 and 1.2 is not affected by surrounding objects. These images are thus used to pinpoint a suitable photometric redshift for the system, with a photo-<em>z</em> around <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a01.8. The confidence interval of this system is formally [0.05\u20133.86]; however, the range below <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.34 is ruled out, since the galaxy must be behind the cluster to be lensed.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaabe7bf2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bf2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Left: image of RXC\u00a0J0142+44 created using a combination of WFC3/IR imaging in the red (F160W) and ACS imaging in the green (F814W) and blue (F435W) filters. The locations of multiply imaged lensed galaxies are overplotted and labeled. The red curve marks the location of the critical curve for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0. The yellow curve marks the location of the critical curve at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0. The image is oriented northeast. Right: the magnification for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0 from the best-fit lens model is shown as contours; contour values are given in the legend. The background colormap indicates the uncertainty level in each location, given as \u0394<em>\u03bc</em>/<em>\u03bc</em>. The uncertainty estimate takes into account the source redshift uncertainty, but does not account for other systematics (see the text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaabe7bf2\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaabe7bf2\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>System #2 consists of one galaxy lensed three times, labeled 2.1\u20132.3. Due to contamination from nearby sources or low signal-to-noise, we were unable to measure a reliable photometric redshift for this system. We therefore set a broad prior on its redshift.</p><p>System #3 is also lensed four times, labeled 3.1\u20133.4. We fix the redshift of the system to <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.1 in order to constrain the redshifts of the other systems in the field. We discuss the implication of this approach in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bs5\">5</a>.</p><p>System #4 has three visible images, labeled 4.1\u20134.3. One additional image is predicted to be west of 3.1 and 3.2, but its predicted magnitude is too faint to be detected in the current data.</p><p>We find that one cluster-scale halo plus galaxy-scale halos are sufficient to reproduce the lensing observables. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt7\">7</a> lists the locations of the images of the lensed galaxies and their redshifts. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt8\">8</a> lists the best-fit parameters of the resulting model.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt8\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 8.</b>\u00a0\nRXC\u00a0J0142.9+4438 Model Parameters\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bt8\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt8_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 8\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Object</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u0394R.A. Position angles are measured north of west, and the ellipticity <em><img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/epsi.gif\" alt=\"epsilon\" align=\"baseline\" /></em> is defined as (<em>a</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>b</em><sup>2</sup>)/(<em>a</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>b</em><sup>2</sup>). Square brackets indicate fixed parameters. <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub> is fixed to 1500 kpc for Halo 1.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt8_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt8_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs4-3\" name=\"apjaabe7bs4-3\">4.3.\u00a0RXC\u00a0J2211.7-0349</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We detect two lensed galaxies in the field of RXC\u00a0J2211.7-0349. Their positions and photometric redshifts are listed in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt5\">5</a>.</p><p>System\u00a0#1 is lensed by the cluster into five multiple images, labeled 1.1\u20131.5 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf3\">3</a>. We note that the demagnified image 1.5, located close to the BCG, is clearly detected in the data, and its colors and morphology match the other images. Its blue color distinguishes it from the BCG light. Images 1.1 and 1.2 were targeted for spectroscopy using a multi-object slit mask with LDSS3 on <em>Magellan</em>, which resulted in a spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>\u00a0=\u00a01.051 based on emission lines from [O <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>], [Ne <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>] 3869, and H<sub><em>\u03b2</em></sub>. The photometric redshifts of these images favor a lower redshift, with a 95% CL range of [0.821\u20130.979], where the highest likelihood is at <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.85. The spectroscopic redshift is outside the 95% CL, but has nonzero BPZ probability for the observed <em>z</em><sub>spec</sub>. In the lensing analysis of this cluster, we use the spectroscopic redshift of source #1 as a fixed constraint.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaabe7bf3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bf3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0Left: image of RXC\u00a0J2211.7-0349, from WFC3/IR imaging in red (F160W) and ACS imaging in green (F814W) and blue (F435W). The locations of multiply imaged arcs are plotted and labeled. The red curve marks the location of the critical curve for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0. The yellow curve marks the location of the critical curve at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0. The image is oriented northeast. Right: the magnification for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0 from the best-fit lens model is shown as contours; contour values are given in the legend. The background colormap indicates the uncertainty level in each location, given as \u0394<em>\u03bc</em>/<em>\u03bc</em>. The uncertainty estimate takes into account the source redshift uncertainty, but does not account for other systematics (see the text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaabe7bf3\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaabe7bf3\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf3\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>System #2 and system #3 are lensed into three images labeled 2.1\u20132.3 and 3.1\u20133.3, respectively. System #3 was targeted for spectroscopy; however, we were unable to secure a spectroscopic redshift from the data.</p><p>We identify an Einstein Cross configuration around a galaxy 90<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />2 from the cluster core at R.A.\u00a0=\u00a022:11:41.986, Decl.\u00a0=\u221203:50:52.31. The F606W-F814W color of the lensing galaxy is redder than the cluster red sequence, likely placing this lens galaxy behind the cluster. The lensing potential of this galaxy is boosted by the nearby lensing potential of the cluster, thus allowing it to reach a critical mass density for strong lensing. The projected distance of this lensing galaxy is far enough from the center of the cluster that it does not significantly affect the cluster lensing potential. We therefore exclude this galaxy and lensed images from the model and leave an analysis of this lensing galaxy to future work.</p><p>We find that two cluster-scale halos are required in order to match the lensing observables, supplemented by galaxy-scale halos. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt9\">9</a> lists the locations of the lensed galaxies and their redshifts. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt10\">10</a> lists the best-fit parameters of the resulting model. The projected mass density of this cluster appears to be a \"warped\" elliptical, with a radius-dependent position angle. This may indicate a more complex dark matter distribution than what may be implied from the galaxy distribution. A multiwavelength and dynamical analysis of this cluster may shed more light on its structure.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt9\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey char=\".\">\u00a0</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> Properties of the images that were used as constraints in the lens model of ACT-CLJ0102-49151. The model-<em>z</em> and rms are given for the best-fit model, and the rms is measured in the image plane for each family of multiple images.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt11_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt11_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>This cluster was previously modeled by Zitrin et. al (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib53\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib53\">2013</a>; hereafter Z13), using ACS imaging data taken as part of GO-12755 (PI: Hughes), in F625W, F775W, and F850LP, and ground-based data. Z13 identifies nine systems and candidate lensed galaxies and uses them to create a Light\u2013Traces\u2013Mass model, as well as a parametric model that uses the same scaling relations as the models in this paper. The new <em>HST</em> imaging data confirms five of these systems and reveals several potential new systems. Where available, we labeled our arcs with the same designation as in Z13 for consistency. These arcs are systems #1, #2, #4, #5, and #9.</p><p>System #1 has two emission knots, labeled 1.1\u20131.3 and 10.1\u201310.3 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf4\">4</a>. Arc system #1 matches the identification of Z13. Arc system #10 is a secondary emission knot in the same system, clearly resolved from #1 in the <em>HST</em> data.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaabe7bf4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bf4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Left: composite color image of ACT-CLJ0102-49151 created using a combination of WFC3IR imaging (red: F160W, green: F105W), and ACS imaging (blue: F775W). The images of lensed galaxies are overplotted and labeled. The red and yellow curves mark the location of the critical curves for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0 and <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0, respectively. The image is oriented northeast. Right: the magnification for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0 from the best-fit lens model is shown as contours; contour values are given in the legend. The background colormap indicates the uncertainty level in each location, given as \u0394<em>\u03bc</em>/<em>\u03bc</em>. The uncertainty estimate takes into account the source redshift uncertainty, but does not account for other systematics (see the text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaabe7bf4\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaabe7bf4\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>System #2 appears as a straight, elongated arc, NW of the southern core of the cluster toward the northern core. The low curvature of this giant arc is indicative of significant lensing potential on both sides, as we see in the mass distribution that was derived for this cluster, as well as in other merging clusters (e.g., the \"Bullet Cluster,\" Brada\u010d et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib7\">2006</a>; Clowe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib9\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib9\">2006</a>). We identify several distinct emission clumps in this arc. Their mapping indicates that the giant arc is a merging pair of two of the images of this system, bisected by the critical curve for the redshift of the arc. The third, much less distorted image of this source is clearly identified and labeled 2.3 and 20.3 in accordance with the Z13 identification.</p><p>System #3 is a newly identified system with three images, labeled 3.1, 3.2, and 3.3.</p><p>System #4 is labeled 4.1, 4.2, and 4.3. Our lensing analysis agrees with the identification of Z13 for arcs Z13-4.1, Z13-4.4, and Z13-4.5; however, we disagree with the identification of arcs Z13-4.2 and candidate arc Z13-c4.3 as being part of the same system. The new <em>HST</em> data shows that the colors of these arcs are much bluer than arcs 4.1\u20134.3, and their predicted positions are inconsistent with our lens model.</p><p>System #5 corresponds to arc candidate c5.3 in Z13. We disagree with the predicted counter image candidate c5.1/2 in Z13, and identify a new image, arc 5.1, based on similar parity, orientation, and colors.</p><p>System #8, labeled 8.1 and 8.2, is a new identification.</p><p>System #9 has three images; 9.1\u20139.2 correspond to arc candidates c9.1 and c9.2 in Z13. We revise the position of 9.3 to be slightly more northwest of candidates c9.3 in Z13; otherwise, the image identifications are the same.</p><p>System #13, labeled 13.1, 13.2, and 13.3, is a new identification, made possible by its distinct IR-Visible colors.</p><p>System #14, labeled 14.1 and 14.2, is also a new identification of a faint pair of arcs near the northern core of the cluster. It was not used as a constraint in the model presented here.</p><p>We find that two cluster-scale halos are needed in order to produce the lensing observables, similar to the previous model of Z13. These halos are located at the two regions that appear to have the densest galaxy distribution in the cluster, in the southeast and in the northwest of the field of view. Z13 noted that the mass ratio between the SE and NW clumps is \u00a01.5:1, an opposite trend from the velocity dispersion measured by Menanteau et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaabe7bbib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaabe7bbib26\">2012</a>. Similarly to Z13, we find that within the strong lensing regime (500 kpc) the SE clump is somewhat more massive than the NW clump, with a projected mass density ratio of 1.19:1. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt11\">11</a> lists the locations of the lensed galaxies and their redshifts. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt12\">12</a> lists the best-fit parameters of the resulting model.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt12\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 12.</b>\u00a0\nACT-CLJ0102-49151 Model Parameters\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bt12\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt12_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 12\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Object</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u0394R.A. xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" Error bars correspond to the 1<em>\u03c3</em> confidence level as inferred from the MCMC optimization. \u0394R.A. and \u0394Decl. are defined in relation to the center of the seventh-brightest cluster galaxy in the field, which serves as the BCG for our lens model. The BCG is located at R.A.\u00a0=\u00a01:02:57.769 and Decl.\u00a0=\u00a0\u221249:16:19.20. Position angles are measured north of west, and the ellipticity <em><img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/epsi.gif\" alt=\"epsilon\" align=\"baseline\" /></em> is defined as (<em>a</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>b</em><sup>2</sup>)/(<em>a</em><sup>2</sup>\u00a0+\u00a0<em>b</em><sup>2</sup>). Square brackets indicate fixed parameters. <em>r</em><sub>cut</sub> is fixed to 1500 kpc for Halo 1.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt12_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt12_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div><h3 id=\"apjaabe7bs4-5\" name=\"apjaabe7bs4-5\">4.5.\u00a0Abell\u00a02163</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Abell\u00a02163 is the most massive cluster in the RELICS survey with an estimated <em>Planck</em> mass <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bieqn77.gif\" alt=\"${M}_{500}=16.12\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{M}_{500}=16.12\\times {10}^{14}\\,{M}_{\\odot }</script></span></span>.</p><p>We identify four lensed galaxies near the core of Abell\u00a02163, each with three images. They are labeled 1.1\u20131.3, 2.1\u20132.3, 3.1\u20133.3, and 4.1\u20134.3 in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaabe7bf5\">5</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaabe7bf5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bf5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf5_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/859/2/159/Full/apjaabe7bf5_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0Left: composite color image of Abell\u00a02163 created using ACS imaging (red: F814W, green: F606W, blue: F435W). The images of lensed galaxies are overplotted and labeled. The locations of the critical curves for sources at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0 and <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0, are marked in red and yellow, respectively. The image is oriented northeast. Right: the magnification for a source at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a09.0 from the best-fit lens model is shown as contours; contour values are given in the legend. The background colormap indicates the uncertainty level in each location, given as \u0394<em>\u03bc</em>/<em>\u03bc</em>. The uncertainty estimate takes into account the source redshift uncertainty, but does not account for other systematics (see the text).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaabe7bf5\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaabe7bf5\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaabe7bf5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>Spectroscopic observations were attempted for this cluster. However, while redshifts were obtained for several cluster-member galaxies, we were unable to measure spectroscopic redshifts for any lensed galaxies used in the model.</p><p>The redshift of arc system #1 is fixed at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a03.0 based on the photometric redshift measurements of arcs 1.1 and 1.2. We note that the peak of the probability distribution function of the photometric redshift of image 1.3 is much lower, at <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.335, but the redshift assumed for the system is within its 95% CL range of [0.227\u20133.492]. The redshift of this system is fixed (and not left as a free parameter) in order to prevent the model from converging on <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a06 for all the lensed systems. Such high redshifts for these lensed galaxies are unreasonable because their images are clearly detected in the F606W and F435W bands, ruling out a high-redshift source.</p><p>We find that one central halo is sufficient to produce the lensing observables. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt13\">13</a> lists the locations of the lensed galaxies and their redshifts. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaabe7bt14\">14</a> lists the best-fit parameters of the resulting model.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt13\" align=\"center\">0.53 [0.44\u20130.68]</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u22ef</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"char\" char=\"+\">\u00a0</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" The model-<em>z</em> and rms are given for the best-fit model, and the rms is measured in the image plane for each family of multiple images.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt13_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/aabe7b\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt13_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaabe7bt14\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 14.</b>\u00a0\nAbell\u00a02163 Model Parameters\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaabe7bt14\" data-toolbar-img=\"/0004-637X/859/2/159/suppdata/apjaabe7bt14_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 14\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col><col align=\"left\" char=\"\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr valign=\"top\">\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\">Object</th>\n<th scope=\"col\" colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u0394R.A.
